Free Talk

Nightly Chats in Autumn 235

— Yu Ming

On the night of August 30th, there was a sudden crackling sound from far and near. For a moment, I didn't have time to think about it and thought that the "resistance" had started again. Soon I understood that it was setting off firecrackers, and then I made up my mind. Then I thought: Is it some kind of solar term again? ... When I saw the newspaper the next day, I realized that last night was a lunar eclipse, and those crackling sounds were our compatriots and non-compatriots (although we all claim to be descendants of the Yellow Emperor, the descendants of Chi You must not have died out, so they are called "non-compatriots"), trying to save the moon from the mouth of the heavenly dog.

A few days before that, the nights were also very lively. Tables were set up everywhere in the streets and alleys, with noodles and watermelons covered with flies, green worms, mosquitoes, and the like. There was also a table of monks chanting: "Hui Zhu Luo Pumi Ya Hong! Om Ya Hong! Hong!" This was releasing flame mouths and performing the ghost feeding ceremony. It was the Ghost Festival, and ghosts and non-ghosts alike ran out from the underworld to see the big world of Shanghai. Benevolent men and women took this opportunity to fulfill their duties as hosts, entrusting the monks to "Om Ya Hong" and flick a few grains of white rice, asking them to eat their fill.

I am a layman and have never paid much attention to the sky and the underworld, but every time this happens, I can't help but feel the transcendence and appropriateness of the thoughts of our compatriots and non-compatriots who are still in the human world. Not to mention anything else, in less than two whole years, the flags of four provinces, or as small as nine islands, have changed. Not only can they not be saved, but even if one wanted to save them, the situation would not allow it. Therefore, the most appropriate thing to do is to save the moon. Even if the firecrackers are set off with a deafening sound, the heavenly dog will never come to bite, and the chief in the moon (if there is a chief) will not come out to forbid it. It is the same with saving people. There are countless victims of war, drought, and locust plagues. How can the common people who are temporarily spared from disaster have a way to save them? Naturally, it is far better to save souls, which is less work and more meritorious, the same as the merit of the Grand Master's Daoist rituals and building pagodas. This is the so-called "If a man does not think far ahead, he will have immediate worries; and the superior man attends to what is great and distant," which is what this means.

Moreover, "Although the cook does not manage the kitchen, the ritual officer does not overstep the sacred vessels to replace him," is also the clear instruction of the ancient sages. State affairs are for the rulers to manage; the common people do not

need to make a fuss. However, the wise emperors and enlightened kings of the past did not despise the common people, but gave them more transcendent freedom and rights, that is, to listen to you specializing in saving the universe and souls. This is the foundation of peace. From ancient times to the present, it has been followed without fail, and it is expected that it will not

be abolished easily in the future. I remember that it was last year, when the Shanghai war had just stopped, and the Japanese soldiers gradually boarded the warships and retreated into the barracks. One night, there was also such a crackling sound. It was still in the midst of the "long-term resistance." The Japanese did not understand our national essence and thought that the tens of thousands of troops had come to recover the lost land. They immediately put up guards and dispatched troops ... There was a commotion, only to realize that we were saving the moon, and they were seeing ghosts. "Oh, oh! Natuboto, that's how it is"! After exclaiming and admiring, they returned to their peaceful state. This year, they didn't even put up guards, probably because they have been influenced by China's spiritual civilization.

"The World I See" 236

— Xu Maoyong

I live on an upper floor, with the windows facing the XX Hospital. Looking down from the window, the first thing that catches my eye is a row of low, tiled-roofed buildings within the hospital grounds, which turn out to be the mortuary. I've always been timid, afraid of anything related to "death." In the countryside, coffins and graves were, needless to say, what I avoided most. Even funeral processions and ancestral temples often made me uneasy. Unexpectedly, this time my residence happened to be so close to a place where death frequently comes and goes. For the first few days, I was very worried, fearing that my heart would never find peace.

Yet, strangely, things didn't turn out as I expected. I've lived here for a full month, and I haven't felt the slightest unease about this transient place of death. I lean out of the window every day, seeing that row of low, tiled-roofed buildings, and often watching lifeless bodies being carried out of them. Yet, I haven't felt a bit of fear. I even enjoy gazing out the window every day, finding solace for my weariness.

This is strange, but I know its origin. Could it be that the hospital did this intentionally? They planted a row of trees behind the mortuary, and then built a fence behind the trees, thus separating the black shed from the building where I live. I don't know the names of those trees. They are leafy, with slender trunks, yet quite tall, taller than the three-story building where I live, so they are very slender, like a modern woman with a small waist. Whenever there's a breeze, they sway gracefully, rustling softly. I suspect they are poplars. Even if they aren't poplars, I'm willing to consider them poplars, because that is very poetic.

The poetic quality is indeed considerable. This row of poplar-like trees, right in front of my window, creates a green curtain. Peeking through the gaps, there are the ancient, elegant black tiles of the roof and the mysterious white cross on the roof, the red walls opposite, the blue sky above...

All this, though it hasn't inspired me to compose any poems, has indeed pleased my eyes and soothed my mind, like gazing at a natural landscape. At least, the black shed, which forms part of the scenery, has completely lost its meaning as a mortuary to me. Even when I often see corpses being carried out, I just regard it as an embellishment to the scenery.

This is a miracle: transforming a fearful and miserable realm into a beautiful and solemn scene. But I know this is due to the "blinding trick" of that row of trees.

Could it be that the hospital did this intentionally? But no matter what, this row of trees is a great gift to me and to the tenants of this three-story building who will come after me, a magic weapon that allows us to find joy in a terrifying realm. I am very grateful to the hospital for planting these trees. I am grateful for more than just this. I am also grateful for the great lesson they have given me, making me realize that all the sufferings of the world can be relieved by "blinding tricks." Natural disasters, man-made calamities, and national crises pile up, yet the people are still cheerful as if ascending a spring terrace. It's not really that they lack passion, but that there are too many things that obscure their view. The earth's fire runs underground, but as long as wild grass grows above, it will make people forget the danger of eruption.

However, there are those whose eyes are covered, those who create their own blinders, and those who simply close their eyes... Different people, each with "the world I see." And the true, objective world is ignored.

The phrase "the world I see," used here, is the title of a book published last year by Emil Ludwig. I have a French translation of this book, which contains this passage about ears and eyes:

"The ear is a woman; when she listens, she is passive. The eye is a man; when he looks, he is able to be independent. Therefore, when the eye does not want to see, he will use the natural method: close. If the ear does not want to hear, it must depend on the artificial method (using both hands to cover them)." This is very true. When my gaze is focused on the beautiful "scenery," ignoring the mortuary, my ears cannot refuse the intrusion of the mournful cries coming from the mortuary. Whenever the night is deep and quiet, the rustling of the leaves of those poplar-like trees often evokes in me a terror and sorrow for death.

After the eyes are covered, we suffer from still having hearing, which allows us to vaguely know the situation of the real world.

Although I also have two hands, for some reason, I never have the courage to raise them to cover my ears.

Further Discussion on Ma Zhiyuan 237

— Zhao Jingshen

Mr. Zheng Zhenduo wrote an article "Ma Zhiyuan's Zaju" in the Free Talk on the 9th, believing that my "The Embryo of Ma Zhiyuan's Zaju" written in July had two errors: (1) Ma's four Xiaoling poems are not necessarily written before the Zaju; therefore, they are not necessarily the embryo of the Zaju. (2) "Meng Haoran Seeking Plum Blossoms in the Snow" was not written by Ma Zhiyuan. I am very happy that he gave me this opportunity so that I can explain my conjecture.

On the first point, I still maintain my original idea that the Xiaoling came first, and the Zaju came later. There are two reasons: (1) The first "Four Pieces of Jade Xunyang River" is not much different from Bai Juyi's "Pipa Ballad." Xunyang River says:

Seeing off guests, the autumn river is cold, the merchant girl's pipa wails. Knowing that Sima listened with sorrow. The moon is bright, the wine is sobering, the guest is awakening. This poem adopted the original meaning of the "Pipa Ballad." The original poem "Pipa Ballad" says:

At Xunyang Riverhead, seeing off guests at night, tree leaves and reed catkins rustle in the autumn wind... Turning the peg and plucking the strings two or three times... a special kind of melancholy and deep hatred arises... Only the white autumn moon can be seen on the river... Jiangzhou Sima's green shirt is wet.

It can be seen that Ma Zhiyuan at that time did not yet have any literary fantasy imagination, but only adopted the poetic meaning for the song. When he wrote "Green Shirt Tears," it was not the same. He let go and added many love

plots out of thin air, completely deviating from the scope of the original poem. If Ma Zhiyuan had first written such arbitrary imagination or borrowing wine to relieve sorrow and creating something out of nothing "Green Shirt Tears," it seems that he would not write such a restrained "Xunyang River," right? As for the Xiaoling being short and enough to develop the Zaju, that is secondary. (2) If "Xunyang River" was written before "Green Shirt Tears," then the remaining two "Four Pieces of Jade" must have been written before "Green Shirt Tears," because in "Taiping Yuefu," these three are placed close together and are all titled with place names (Tiantai Road, Zizhi Road), and should be works of the same period. Moreover, these three are all "Four Pieces of Jade" and are all stories of the Zaju that Ma Zhiyuan wrote, so I cannot help but arouse suspicion and speculation. In addition, what Mr. Zheng said, that the Xiaoling of the Yuan people chanting Chen Bo and Meng Haoran, and the Xiaoling of the Yuan and Ming people singing the story of Cui Zhang, are not the embryos of Ma Zhiyuan and Wang Bao's operas; it only increases the rhetoric. In fact, I have never said that other people's Xiaoling are the embryos of Ma Zhiyuan's Zaju, and there is no need to use this kind of comparison.

On the second point, I also saw him say this in Zheng's History of Chinese Literature, page 872: "The Xiji Zi Zaju Selection also contains his book 'Meng Haoran Seeking Plum Blossoms in the Snow,' but that was written by Zhu Zhouxian, King of Zhou, in the Ming Dynasty, not by him." Recently, he said in Free Talk: "We cannot find a play called 'Seeking Plum Blossoms in the Snow' in the most ancient records of the Record of Ghosts and the Taihe Zheng Yin Pu in Ma's drama list." But I

checked the "Taihe Zheng Yin Pu" reproduced by the Ancient Books Circulation Office, page 12, line 6 of the upper volume, under the "Zaju Compiled by Qunying" Ma Zhiyuan entry, there is the play title "Seeking Plum Blossoms in the Snow." (The preface of the Yuan Qu Selection and Liang Tingnan's Qu Hua both quote it) The Qu Yuan edition of Zhong Sicheng's Lu Gui Bu, page 9 of the Six Arts Book Bureau, also has "Seeking Plum Blossoms in the Snow." Chen Naigan's Qu Lu School Supplement in the 10th issue of Jian Shang Zhou Kan (August 1925) said: "Or it is said that Meng Haoran Seeking Plum Blossoms in the Snow should be attributed to Yuan Ma Zhiyuan according to the Yishi Garden Catalog. However, many Zaju titles of Yuan and Ming people are the same, or slightly embellished, or the plot is changed. For example, the Qu Jiang Chi of Cheng Qi Yuefu is also written by Shi Junshi of Yuan, with the same name but different Guanmu." He said that "Guanmu is actually different" means admitting that Ma has another script writing about the same event. In the same example, the ending of the fourth act of Ma

Zhiyuan's "Liu Ruan Mistakenly Entering Taoyuan Cave" (recorded in the Bei Ci Guang Zheng Pu and Taihe Zheng Yin Pu) cannot be found in Wang Ziyi's "Liu Chen Ruan Zhao Mistakenly Entering Taoyuan." I think that if the "Seeking Plum Blossoms in the Snow" selected by Xiji Zi is completely the same as that of Zhou Xianwang, then Ma's is probably lost, so Xiji Zi came to a case of Zhang Guan Li Dai after reading books such as Lu Gui Bu and Taihe Zheng Yin Pu, which is not necessarily a "familiar reading of Xiaoling." Wang Guowei clearly stated under the entry "Seeking Plum Blossoms in the Snow": "Taihe Zheng Yin Pu" has this book." I think this may be a temporary oversight error by Mr. Zheng. Taihe Zheng Yin Pu recorded only thirteen kinds of Ma Zhiyuan's Zaju, including "Seeking Plum Blossoms in the Snow." Removing the collaborative "Yellow Millet Dream" from Qu Lu and adding "Meng Haoran Riding a Donkey in the Snow" and ("Ren Fengzi") only yields fourteen kinds. Mr. Zheng said in the History of Chinese Literature that Ma's Zaju has "fourteen books" (page 869). If "Seeking Plum Blossoms in the Snow" is not included, I am afraid that the number cannot be made up, right?

Shallow Lake (3) 238

— Written by Joseph Conrad, Translated by Shi Heng

In the dim light of the house, he saw a woman lying supine on a bamboo bed, under a wide red cotton quilt. She lay quietly, like a dead person; but her big eyes, wide open, flashed in the dark, her eyes were still, as if she couldn’t see anything, staring at the beams on the roof. She had a very high fever and was obviously unconscious. Her cheeks were slightly sunken, her lips were half-open, and a sinister death-like expression appeared on her young face—the unintentional contemplation and dazed expression of a dying person. The two men looked down at her in silence.

"Has she been sick for a long time?" asked the traveler.

"I haven't slept for five nights," the Malay answered in a deep voice. "At first she heard voices calling her in the water. I held her, and she struggled in my arms. But since this morning, she can't hear anything anymore—she can't even hear my voice. She can't see anything anymore. Not even me—she can't even see me!"

He was silent for a while, then asked softly: "Tuan, will she die?"

"Maybe," said the white man sadly. He had known Assat for many years, in a faraway country, in a dangerous and turbulent period, when any friendship was precious. Later, his Malay friend unexpectedly lived in this shallow lake cabin with a strange woman. He had stayed here many times during his journey along this river. He liked this native because he knew how to keep his word and how to stand by his white friend and fight fearlessly. He loved him, perhaps as a person loves his beloved dog, but he could still give him aid and love him without any expectation, even in his own busy career, he would vaguely think of this lonely man hiding in the forest with fear and the long-haired, arrogant-looking woman with a pair of victorious eyes.

The white man walked out of the cabin, just in time to see a black, turbulent cloud rising between the treetops, and the shadow that came quickly and stealthily spread across the sky, diluting the deep red of the floating clouds and the red light of the end of the day, and annihilating the huge flames of the setting sun. After a while, stars appeared in the thick darkness of the earth, and the shallow lake, shimmering with starlight, was like an oval night sky cast into a desolate wilderness of dismal black night. The white husband took out some dinner food from the basket, gathered some branches scattered on the platform, and lit a small fire, not for warmth, but to drive away mosquitoes with the smoke. He wrapped his body in a blanket, sat there leaning against the reed wall of the house, and smoked thoughtfully.

Assat walked out of the door without a sound and squatted beside the fire. The white man moved his outstretched legs.

"She is panting," Assat said softly. "She is panting and feels like she is being burned by a big fire. She doesn't speak, she doesn't listen, just the fire burns!"

He paused for a while, then asked quietly and indifferently: "Tuan...will she die?"

The white man moved his shoulder uneasily, and murmured hesitantly, as if hesitating: "If that is her fate."

"No, Tuan," Assat said calmly. "If that is my fate. I listen, I watch, I wait and wait. I remember...Tuan, do you remember the old days? Do you remember my brother?"

Gold and Silver Prices Rebound One Dollar and Ten Cents 239

Silver and Commodity Prices Rise and Fall

Short Covering Near Expiry Results in Rebound

After a downward trend in the gold market since the previous day, yesterday, the overseas telegraph reported that both the British and American silver markets rose, the British and American exchange rates increased by 2.625 points, the American and British exchange rates increased by 2.375 points, the forward silver price on the Metal Exchange increased by 5.2 to 6.5 points, the private telegram silver price increased by 5.625 points, American cotton increased by 20 pounds, stocks increased by 4.17 dollars, American wheat increased by 3 points, and the London spot gold price decreased by 5 pence. The gross price immediately broke through 20 dollars and continued to retreat to 15 dollars, but it recovered due to large buyers taking advantage of the low price to buy in. After opening, it once again broke through the 20-dollar mark, but it gradually rose due to the healthy appetite of the banks. Although it slightly declined afterward, it mostly hovered. Retail customers squeezed prices, once decreasing to 20 dollars, but the noon closing price remained stable. There were also rumors that coal industry regulations had progressed. Banks were blocked and broke through 20 dollars, but it gradually stabilized due to eager short covering. Securities 244

New Government Bond Rumors Dominate

The Bond Market Lingers, Ending Slightly Better

Yesterday, the Chinese Merchants Securities Exchange saw slight changes in trends. Generally speaking, each trading board experienced a slight increase. The standard for current rises and falls is focused on whether new government bonds will be issued. There is much debate in the market, with some saying that 120 million in new government bonds will be issued to make up for financial shortfalls. However, those familiar with the inside story believe that issuing new government bonds would be extremely difficult to unload, and the benefits to the government would be limited. Therefore, it is unlikely that things will develop in this way. Speculation abounds, but for many days, most have believed that selling short is advisable. The number of short sellers in the market has gradually increased, creating a crowding effect. A slight rebound immediately leads to a rise. The first trading board was generally stable with a slight increase, but unified salt tax bonds were still being sold, falling by 5 to 20 cents. The second trading board was initially chaotic, with ups and downs, but the volume was very small. Unified salt tax bonds rebounded by about 10 cents. Although the 31st series and others were still being sold, buyers gradually emerged. The afternoon opening saw a unanimous increase of 10 to 20 cents, and the closing remained firm, continuing to improve by 10 to 20 cents. As a result, except for the 1929 Customs bonds, which were slightly down by 5 cents, the rest rebounded by 10 to 55 cents. Judging from the overall trend, there are many short positions, and there may be a possibility of continued increases. The total transaction volume was 6,216,000 yuan, including 1,000 yuan in spot transactions. August Sees Strong Sales of Japanese Yarn in Shanghai 251

丨丨Influence of Rising Prices of Three-Grade Yarn丨丨

At the end of last month, the inventory of Japanese yarn in this port, although not thoroughly investigated, was approximately 10,000 bales less than the inventory at the end of July (34,000 bales). This was due to the surge in the price of three-grade yarn at the beginning of last month. Trading houses from the Northeast and Tianjin purchased very actively, with approximately 3,500 bales of 16s and 20s yarn being sold. Later, demand in various regions weakened, and the price of yarn fell along with the decline in the Chinese cotton market. In the middle of the month, U.S. cotton rebounded, and Tianjin houses began to purchase again, leading to competitive buying from various trading houses in Qingdao, Hankou, and this port. As a result, the situation changed dramatically, and the market price soared, with more than 15,000 bales being transacted. By the end of the month, the price of three-grade yarn rose again, and Japanese companies purchased 8,000 bales from Japanese factories in Shanghai. Therefore, the strong sales of Japanese yarn in the middle of last month were unprecedented in recent months, and a sharp reduction in inventory can be predicted.

Grains 255

The Goods are Clean, Fragrant, and the Price Opens at 7.80 Yuan

(South Shanghai) Yesterday, there were more than 70 sources, and both wholesale and retail appetites were similar to before. However, with the continued influx of goods, sentiment weakened further, so the situation was flat. In total, Yantai trading houses had more than 1,000 packages, and the prices of other thick japonica rice, thin indica rice, Duyang new pointed rice, etc., continued to decline by more than a dime. The exchange rate changed from negative to fixed. The prices of new inland river japonica rice were not significantly different, and the prices of new Shandong rice remained unchanged. As for inland river fragrant japonica rice, it was launched yesterday. The goods are clean and fragrant. Since the first day is still the first day, customers are competing to buy them, so the market is quite lively and the price opens at 7.80 yuan.

(North Shanghai) Yesterday, there were approximately 37-38 sources from various river routes. Sales in the market were sluggish due to the intermittent cloudy and sunny weather, so appetites were light. The price of white japonica rice was slightly down, the price of early thin indica rice was slightly down by nearly a dime, the price of new Yang pointed and round pointed rice was slightly down by a dime, and the price of new Bu pointed rice was down by about two dimes. New Ke Indica Rice Continues to Rise, Up by a Dime or So 256

The Ke indica rice market was very good yesterday because only the railway route has arrivals recently. Although Hunan rice transported by boat has arrived, it is all sold at a limited price due to high costs. The producers are concerned that arrivals will be difficult to be strong in the future due to unfavorable production prices. Foreign rice prices have also been raised by the cargo owners, but traders have not been able to close deals due to high asking prices. However, Ke rice merchants have a strong appetite because they are unable to trade Hunan and foreign rice smoothly, so they are paying more attention to Nanjing railway indica rice. Quanzhou merchants from Fujian province have the strongest appetite. Yesterday, merchants from Beiyang also arrived in the city to test-buy more than 100 packages of new Nanjing indica rice. Merchants from Wenzhou and Taizhou, who have not purchased for a long time, also inquired about Nanjing brown rice yesterday. Therefore, the market situation is very good. The price of brown rice rose by a dime, and the price of polished rice rose by five cents. Currently, the total inventory of new Ke indica rice is approximately 10,000 packages. If Ke demand is strong again today and tomorrow, the market will still need to take steps.

Factory Dumping Intensifies, Flour Prices Plunge 257

New substitute price for this month is 2.2125 yuan

Yesterday, the flour market opened in the morning with rising prices due to strong actual sales the previous day and foreign wheat prices rising by one yuan. Sentiment was upward, and short positions were covered. Prices for each month in the near term rose by several cents, and prices for more distant months were also stable. However, inventories were full, and the sales of more than 100,000 packages did not help. Furthermore, sales to customers did not continue to be strong, and the market was volatile, further weakening sentiment. Fuxin and other major factories took the opportunity to sell, and short selling in the near term was even stronger. As customers and new short sellers saw factories selling off, they also competed to sell more distant months. Therefore, prices for all months, near and far, plunged across the board. The new low price of 2.2125 yuan was seen again for this month. The closing prices for September and October were down by a penny and a half, November was down by a penny and three-quarters, and December and January were each down by a penny.

Wheat Prices Fall Following Flour Prices 258

Therefore, sentiment was very good, and some short positions were covered. Prices for each month were showing signs of prosperity. Following the sudden drop in flour prices, traders hedged their standard contracts for this month, and all had plans to deliver spot. Therefore, sentiment weakened again, and the contract for this month was sold off by traders. The closing price for this month was suddenly down by four cents, the next month was down by two cents, and November and December were each down by one cent. (Silk Sales in Europe and America Plummet) The European and American raw silk markets are sluggish, factory sales are slow, and silk prices are slightly down, in a state of continuous decline. American silk merchants are holding onto goods with no inquiries, and they are nitpicking about the raw silk deliveries from Chinese merchants, often lowering prices or even breaking contracts. The future of American sales is increasingly bleak. Although European traders are covering short positions and trading, opening prices are increasingly weak. Yesterday, only Renji and others traded 25 packages of yellow and white factory silk, and prices remained flat and weak.

Essays

People are Not as Good as Ghosts - Person 265

In the past, the area under the overpass, where beggars lay like zombies every night, was frighteningly dark and eerie. But tonight is different. The electric lights shine brighter than white paper, and this "old but not dead is a thief" old man can barely open his eyes. In addition to the bright electric lights, there's also a stage. They say they're going to do something called "Tanhuang" later. The words "Tanhuang" are quite unfamiliar to me. A year ago, I had never been to this so-called "ten-mile foreign concession" of Shanghai from my village. I had only heard of Shanghai's "Bund" and "foreign coppers" -- those famous portraits of "foreign masters." "Tanhuang" is a new word that I'm hearing for the first time in my life. I think to myself, since this stage is set up under the overpass, surely I can watch it for free. Driven by curiosity, I steel myself and wait to see what the civilization of Shanghai, the authentic ten-mile foreign concession, is like, something that my village doesn't have.

The hour and minute hands pass by, and the minute hand is already pointing at twelve. My old eyes are really tired, but the thought of the strangely new word "Tanhuang" makes me feel a bit more awake. Just then, I quickly see a man and a woman go up on stage to perform. After listening for a long time, all I hear are things related to "men and women," things that people in my village are absolutely forbidden to talk about. There's nothing else. Ah... so-called "Tanhuang" is just this. I dare not learn any more. I think to myself, people pay money to have these guys, who are neither actors nor anything else, perform such "obscene" acts. What's the point?

When I get to my doorstep, I hear my eldest granddaughter arguing that she wants to go out to see the "Tanhuang" that's going on over there. My daughter-in-law says, "How can a girl watch that kind of 'Tanhuang'? Only lowlifes watch that." I hear all this, and I don't say a word. I think to myself that she's a good daughter-in-law, knowing that "Tanhuang" isn't worth watching and forbidding her daughter from going. This is truly a blessing for our family. I drag a friend from the same alley and ask him, "What's going on over there? Why is it so lively?" "It's the Ghost Festival in July, a Taoist rite. Because the living are too 'poor' now, the dead are naturally also very 'poor'. So when the hungry ghosts are released from hell in July, they really need everyone to donate some money to buy tinfoil and burn it into 'silver' for them. Now, they're putting on a show for the ghosts." Ah! So it's a Taoist rite. This reminds me of the group of people who looked like beggar ghosts who came to my house yesterday to ask for donations. Because their so-called righteous words gave me a headache, I gave them a "Zhongshan head" -- that's the price of my old man's sweat and blood! Who knew they would use it to put on this kind of show? Shanghai is really easy to "fall for"! I really don't understand, does putting on a show like this really give the dead ghosts blessings and "deliver" them? Really, in this day and age, people are not as good as ghosts. This old man still has to work like a horse all day long, and I've never heard of anyone wanting to give me any blessings or save me. Ghosts, on the other hand, have compassionate gentlemen with bodhisattva hearts willing to "deliver" them. Really, in this day and age, no one is going to "deliver" or "save" this group of us who are sweating and bleeding. All we hear and encounter are increased oppression and burdens. But ah, are we willing to accept this?

In the Brothel - Lie 266

丨I am a person, I am even more a young girl丨

In such seemingly integrated combination, in such closely-related lives, no one would have thought that they were so different at heart, with such a vicious chasm dividing them, like a first wife wielding real power lording over a concubine, but here it is filled with the temptation of money, and no sour mockery.

Ah Ying, in the madam's mouth, is a particularly strange prostitute, and the most heartless. For example, during the January 28th Incident last year, when the madam was ill and unable to supervise her, she also pretended to be sick and didn't go out. Sometimes, she would spend the whole day and night saying she was going to the Suzhou Creek to see the excitement. When she was called out to do business at night, she would use the excuse of martial law, saying that there was simply no one walking on the streets. During the day, she would just loaf around all day, and it didn't matter if she didn't turn in any money. She would even get angry: "Do you think there's business to be done during the day? The airplanes are rattling in the sky so much, and the atmosphere is so tense, who has the leisure or the money?"

The madam hated her thoroughly. For an entire month, she only turned in forty yuan. When she was asked about it, she would immediately get angry.

The madam was grateful that "good fortune shone on her" and that she was finally free of her illness with the final cannon fire of the Japanese soldiers attacking Zhabei.

She went out, and acquaintances all complimented her: "Your Ah Ying seems to have changed recently. She's very generous!" Lao Si said it most vividly: One day, he saw her riding in a car on the street, and another day, he saw her with a young white face going to a certain big hotel. He also found out how she was enticing the young white face, making him cling to her, letting her manipulate him, playing "being kept" like a poodle.

When the madam heard this, she was horrified. She had never dreamed that little Ah Ying was involved in such a thing. Ah, no wonder she had completely changed. When she did business, she always said that she had been standing on the street all day, and she used the excuse of martial law at night to stay at home. It turned out she was being kept by a young white face outside.

"Ah Ying, you're so bold, daring to play tricks in front of me. Tell me truthfully, tell me truthfully about your loafing around this month!"

"Nothing, haven't I been reporting it every day! I made three yuan one day, and I didn't get any business another day." Ah Ying was a little frightened. She realized that as soon as the madam got better, she would be taking it out on them again, otherwise, where would the medical expenses come from?

Ah Ying was thinking to herself: Only the madam's lover, Hu Mazi, had introduced her to an old military officer named Zhao. He had a full beard and was so old, but he still pretended to be young. She reluctantly spent a night with him, and he still kept pestering her afterwards. But that time, she turned in the money according to the rules, it was just that she secretly pocketed the extra bit that Old Zhao gave her. Could that be it? Tell me truthfully, could that be it!

As for having some dealings with Young Wang, I'd need to have such abilities, and I am a young girl, and I spend my own money. Is it destined in our young girls' lives that we are only to be played with by dead men like Old Zhao? Absolutely not!

Sister and Miss

Ah Ying was pondering, not answering, and the madam hit her to the ground with a stick. Then many onlookers began to kick and punch her.

Ah Ying struggled to defend herself, shouting:

"I am a person! I am even more a young girl!"

Autumn Clouds - Preface by Qian 267

How can I not miss it, this day a year ago! At that time, summer had just passed, the intense heat replaced by the coolness of autumn. A gentle breeze of early autumn blew on people, causing an inexplicable comfort. Outside Fengrun Gate in the capital, with clear lake water on both sides and green mountains in the distance, a long embankment stretched out, planted with [space left blank in original]. The autumn cicadas were singing their sorrows above people's heads. However, neither she nor I felt any sense of solemnity. Our hearts were filled only with emotions as warm and fervent as those of a gentle spring.

At that moment, we were strolling on the long embankment, each silently enjoying the gifts of nature. Suddenly, a white cloud flew from the east, resembling an elephant with a long trunk, but after several rotations, it suddenly transformed into a divine dragon with bared teeth and claws. She looked up and couldn't help but sigh, "Autumn clouds are so ever-changing, seeing it now, I truly believe it!"

"You're about to become literary," I said with a smile. Suddenly, a sense of melancholy washed over my heart: "The changes of human affairs are probably even greater!"

My face changed from [space left blank in original] to [space left blank in original]. My heart seemed shrouded in a dark shadow, and the weight of that shadow seemed to grow heavier and heavier, so heavy that I couldn't breathe.

She seemed to sense something was amiss, but she didn't reveal it, because she knew that dwelling on things would only make the situation worse and would only be detrimental to me. So, she said with a faint smile:

"Your words are somewhat seemingly true but actually false. Among my many classmates, among my many relatives, although there are some who change very quickly, they are in the minority. Most of them are progressing smoothly... Moreover, in the attitude of a revolutionary youth, one should only grasp reality and not dwell on the future, especially not be pessimistic about the future. Yu! Be optimistic, our future is the brightest."

Her gentle attitude, her generous words, her fiery passion, made me feel excited, and the shadow in my heart disappeared without a trace. We walked hand in hand and stopped under a large willow tree.

"Is it okay to sit here?"

"Very good."

So, we took out a handkerchief, spread it on the ground, and sat down leaning against each other. The shade of the willow tree covered us, and a gust of wind blew from across the way, tousling her short hair. We talked, we laughed, we looked at the white clouds flying overhead for a while, we looked at the mountain scenery in the distance for a while, and we looked at the yachts in the lake for a while. At this time, we were almost completely intoxicated by nature.

Suddenly, a light and delicate voice came from behind us: "Sir, Miss, would you like to take a boat to play in the lake?"

When I turned around and saw clearly that it was a boat girl, I asked for her consent. She nodded in agreement, and we jumped onto the boat one after the other. The boat girl poked the punt pole against the shore, and the boat slowly moved towards the depths of the lotus pond. This poetic situation made people forget everything, and she couldn't help but sing softly. How deep that day's impression was on me! Now, driven by the whip of life, I have drifted to Shanghai. Everything feels noisy and turbid. As for her, because I haven't heard from her for a long time, I don't know what her situation is? The changes of human affairs are even greater than those of the autumn cicadas!

Shen Bao Monthly

Gleanings from Changsha - A Changsha Native 268

The [Shanghai] rickshaws, the [blank space in original] rickshaws, and the Changsha rickshaws are equally crowded. Walking on the streets, all I hear is the "He Nan! He Nan!" sound filling my ears. This is the sound of the rickshaw pullers [blank space in original] pedestrians [blank space in original]. What these words mean, I can't figure out. They are all very honest laborers squeezed out of the countryside, and their prices are very fair. They are living at a very low standard.

X X X X X

There are no "bums" there, but there are "ruffians." There are often such noises in the streets and alleys: "Ruffian, I'll spit a mouthful of thick phlegm at you!" or "Son of a bitch, bastard!" They even escalate into full-blown fights, grappling in a ball. In the deep alleys at night, it is inevitable to "set a price point"! Just like the "pig butchers" of Shanghai, it's terrifying robbery.

X X X X X

The most striking figures on the streets are students. Whether it's sunny or rainy, whether it's male or female, everyone has a fancy umbrella in their hand (a more advanced and elegant paper umbrella). This is the most distinctive mark of the students.

The boys wear twill student uniforms, and the girls wear foreign cloth blouses and skirts. There are no Western suits, and no "tuk, tuk" sounds of high heels. This simple dress has a kind of simple and elegant flavor, charm, and does not detract from the masculinity of the men or the beauty of the women.

X X X X X

However, in recent years, their studies and thoughts have become increasingly strange, clumsy, and backward. Perhaps this is because "those who are near vermilion get stained red," due to their environment. For example, outside of class, they mostly read old antiques such as "Ancient Prose Style" and "Selections of Refined Literature." In class, they "read the classics" and "recite history." As a result, their thinking has stagnated, narrowed, and even become completely confused. The men only hope to rise rapidly in the world, get rich, and become officials, while the women mostly yearn for the inhuman enjoyment of being a concubine. At most, they just want to be a "virtuous wife and loving mother," dependent on men.

X X X X X

In the evening, the sound of "ding-dang... ding... ding-dang" of the charter rickshaws echoes through the streets. Inside sit either vigorous young military officers or civil officials with bearded cheeks, or flower-decked girls and powdered mistresses. Behind the rickshaws, there are often guards with peeled-shell guns at their waists running alongside.

X X X X X

Although there are no dance halls, and the cinemas are also very shoddy, there are large-scale elevated stages and dance floors. It's just that the wealthiest people are most interested in [space left blank in original] becoming depraved. [space left blank in original]. X X X X X

Brother Qiu Ren has great power and is definitely not as unrespected as those in Shanghai. They often barge straight ahead on the streets, haggling hard when shopping. Grouped in threes and fives, they make people afraid to approach because they only know how to say "this" and "that," and don't reason at all.

X X X X X

People there don't have much interest in sightseeing, because the natural environment is too monotonous. The gardens are desolate, and the unremarkable Tianxin Pavilion and Yuelu Mountain across the river are considered places to wander around. In fact, they all inevitably disappoint people after you visit them.

X X X X X

In the middle of the night, in the quiet stillness, the sound of the night watchman's clapper, "bang, bang, bang," permeates the hawkers' cries of "white sugar lotus seed porridge ba," echoing in the deep alleys, which is most unbearable to listen to.

X X X X X

What makes people most reminiscent of the past and the future is that, in recent years, the police power on the streets has often been replaced by soldiers with loaded guns and horse blades (sabers). Not to mention martial law during commemorative holidays, even normally, soldiers often stand guard on the streets for long periods, one every few feet, requiring them to stand with their legs apart and pedestrians being subject to inspection at any time, extremely revealing the terror of the times.

The Carnivorous World - Xin 269

Some of my housemates are working at their desks, some are playing mahjong, some are playing the phonograph, and some are listening to the radio. In addition, the vendors in the alley are still raising their voices to sell their wares, so the quiet night is still disturbed by sounds, just like the waves of ether.

I hate being disturbed the most, so I hide alone in my small room. After finishing my diary, I take out the dried mud fish that my aunt brought from the countryside and chew on it. At that time, the lights in the room are off! I lie on the bed and chew it carefully. It really tastes delicious! After eating one, all that's left is the head! Ah! I am horrified, I dare not eat it anymore. Because this is the head of the dead! Am I really such a cruel carnivorous animal? So, I quickly and forcefully throw it out the window, right onto the tinplate of the workshop downstairs, making a loud bang. I feel even more chilled, realizing that the head I threw down was so big that it could have such a big reaction!

I begin to realize that this world is a carnivorous world! Yes, the law of the jungle has almost become an unchanging principle. Therefore, if we want to survive and not have our own flesh eaten, we must rise up and effectively resist the invasion of the strong. If we only know how to "be respectful" and "make concessions," then we are weak! We will ultimately be swallowed alive, caught, killed like dried mud fish, dried, chewed in the mouth, and finally discarded its useless head and bones!

Modern Celebrities' Paintings and Calligraphy - Miss by Mr. Xu Ju'an

Xu Rong, styled Ju'an, also known as Danxiang An, is a native of Tongxiang, Zhejiang. He has loved painting and poetry since childhood. By the time he reached adulthood, his poetry and painting were well-known throughout Zhejiang. His figures and ladies take the style of Yu Tai Xiaolou, and his skill is particularly unique. He also occasionally paints Buddhist images, which are different from other contemporary artists. After the age of forty, he lived in Shanghai and amused himself with painting in his spare time. He heard that many people were seeking his works, but he was always troubled by not being able to respond widely.

Shop Employee Communications 270

Can He Be Ordered to Move Elsewhere?

Editor Sir:

I am a small clerk with shallow knowledge. Now, because of a very difficult matter at home that I cannot resolve, I specifically ask for your guidance.

My father had three brothers. Since my late grandparents passed away, they had already split up and established their own households, which was quite harmonious. Unfortunately, my second uncle passed away last year, leaving behind a wife and a daughter, who depend on each other for survival. Recently, my second aunt was seduced by a rogue and committed adultery, openly living together, and their feelings for each other are extremely strong. As a result, scandalous rumors spread everywhere. She even claimed that my father was the one who spread the rumors and constantly spoke to him with malice. The other day, because of a trivial matter, an argument broke out, and she even gathered a group of rogues, armed with weapons, to break into our house and destroy our furniture. My father resisted slightly, and in the chaos, her daughter's face was slightly injured, resulting in bleeding. At this point, the other party made a mountain out of a molehill. A person named Zhang, who is now a teacher at a school and has many connections with people in the court, instigated them to arrest my father for the crime of assault. Fortunately, thanks to the persuasion of others, he was spared litigation. But since then, the other party has become even more reckless, and it is truly unbearable to live with them. Now, I plan to order her to move elsewhere. I don't know if the law allows it. When moving, can we take away the ancestral inherited farmland? I hope you can provide detailed instructions on both matters. I am truly grateful. Special.
